<script>
	function goToTopic(topic) {
		var topicMap = applySpecialCharacterMapping(topic); 
		var url = "/xpl/topicbrowse.jsp?topic=" + escape(topicMap);
		window.top.location.href = url;
	}
</script>

The RFID reader antenna can work at near- and far-field operation within the European UHF (865-868 MHz) band. The operation frequency and radiation properties can be modified by employing varactor diodes. Also, the antenna can work in the near-field region having a flat magnetic distribution in the interrogation zone. A comparative study with other passive RFID reader conventional antennas shows that the left-handed loop achieves stronger near H-field with good impedance matching. Design details, simulated results, and a fabricated prototype are presented. The concept significantly extends the design degrees of freedom for RFID antennas.</div>

<div id="BodyWrapper" class="ArticlePage" xmlns:ieee="http://www.ieeexplore.ieee.org"><div id="article">
<div class="section" id="sec1"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION I.</div><h2>Introduction</h2></div><p>In recent years, significant research has been conducted in the area of ultrahigh-frequency (UHF) near/far-field radio frequency identification (RFID). RFID technology has gained popularity for a variety of applications such as contactless payment, metro tickets, keyless vehicle ignition systems, supply chain management, security, or tracking items <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref1" id="context_ref_1_1">[1]</a>, <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref2" id="context_ref_2_1">[2]</a>. Near- or far-field operation is used reliant on the tag and application characteristics. Near-field operation can be useful for objects surrounded by metals and/or liquids in their vicinity, and far-field interaction is commonly used to achieve long read range. For this reason, there is significant research interest in developing antennas that can be used in these systems <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref3" id="context_ref_3_1">[3]</a>–<a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref4" id="context_ref_4_1">[4]</a><a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref5" id="context_ref_5_1">[5]</a><a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref6" id="context_ref_6_1">[6]</a><a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref7" id="context_ref_7_1">[7]</a>. Left-handed metamaterials operating at microwaves frequencies could also be applied in RFID applications. Generally, left-handed antennas are created by assembling a periodic structure composed of elements that are small in size compared to the wavelength of the propagating electromagnetic wave. Consequently, the properties of these artificial materials no longer depend exclusively on the properties of the constitutive elements. Instead, they depend on the properties of the whole macrostructure thus formed. The resulting material can be engineered to exhibit novel electromagnetic properties and to achieve behaviors that are not found with conventional materials.</p><p>In this letter, we present a novel loop antenna incorporating a ladder network with left-handed loading. The antenna exhibits the unique feature of antiparallel phase and group velocity along with zero propagation constant at a certain frequency <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref8" id="context_ref_8_1">[8]</a>–<a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref9" id="context_ref_9_1">[9]</a><a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref10" id="context_ref_10_1">[10]</a><a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref11" id="context_ref_11_1">[11]</a>. In particular, the propagation constant of an artificial transmission line can reach zero values at frequencies where the phase advance and delay offsets cancel. Making use of this phenomenon, electrically small antennas with several operating modes <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref12" id="context_ref_12_1">[12]</a>–<a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref13" id="context_ref_13_1">[13]</a><a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref14" id="context_ref_14_1">[14]</a> can be developed. More specifically, the loop antenna has been designed to exhibit zeroth-order mode operation <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-1-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1" role="math" style="width: 3.607em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 3.246em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1003.13em 2.646em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-2"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-3" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">(</span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-4"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-5"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-6" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">n</span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-7" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">=</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-8" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">0</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-9" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">)</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.33em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.27em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-1">({n}=0)</script></tex-math></inline-formula> at a frequency of 868 MHz. The main advantage of zeroth-order mode operation includes the ability to obtain a uniform current distribution that is independent of the loop length, reconfigurable performances, and strong magnetic near-field distributions.</p><p>This letter is organized as follows. <a ref-type="sec" anchor="sec2" class="fulltext-link">Section II</a> discusses the antenna design of the passive UHF reader left-handed loop antenna. <a ref-type="sec" anchor="sec3" class="fulltext-link">Sections III</a> and <a ref-type="sec" anchor="sec4" class="fulltext-link">IV</a> present the main properties of the structure in the near and far fields. The performance is also compared to that of other conventional right-handed antennas. Finally, the main conclusions of the study and future possible applications are outlined in <a ref-type="sec" anchor="sec5" class="fulltext-link">Section V</a>.</p></div>
<div class="section" id="sec2"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION II.</div><h2>Loop Antenna Design</h2></div><p><a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig1" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 1(a)</a> shows the loop antenna. The antenna is loaded by a left-handed ladder network composed of four unit cells. Moreover, <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig1" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 1(b)</a> shows a prototype that was fabricated using a mechanical milling machine (LPKF Protomat S100). The FR4 has a thickness of 1.5 mm, a permittivity of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-2-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-10" role="math" style="width: 3.847em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 3.426em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.384em 1003.43em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-11"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-12"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-13"></span></span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-14"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.784em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.426em 1000.36em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-15" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">ϵ</span><span style="display: inline-block; The capacitors <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-8-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-62" role="math" style="width: 1.444em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.264em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.264em 1001.26em 2.465em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-63"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-64"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.264em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1000.78em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-65" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">C<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.724em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-66"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-67"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-68" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">L</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.197em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-8">C_{\rm L}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> are introduced into the arm of the ladder network that also incorporates the feeding point. This leads to a difference in the amplitudes of currents <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-9-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-69" role="math" style="width: 0.964em; For this reason, these out-of-phase currents do not completely cancel in the far field, and as a result, they radiate. Thus, the proposed antenna allows size reduction while maintaining good impedance matching by the adjustment of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-11-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-83" role="math" style="width: 1.324em; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.246em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.254em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-14">L_{\rm L}=200 </script></tex-math></inline-formula>nH, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-15-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-115" role="math" style="width: 4.368em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 3.442em; height: 0px; font-size: 126%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.392em 1003.38em 2.45em -999.997em); top: -2.245em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-116"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-117" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">a</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-118" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.268em;">=</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-119" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.268em;">72.3</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.252em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.079em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.088em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-15">a=72.3</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-16-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-120" role="math" style="width: 4.368em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 3.442em; height: 0px; font-size: 126%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.392em 1003.38em 2.45em -999.997em); border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.088em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-16">d=14.1</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-17-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-125" role="math" style="width: 3.575em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.847em; height: 0px; font-size: 126%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.392em 1002.85em 2.45em -999.997em); top: -2.245em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-126"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-127" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">r</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-128" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.268em;">=</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-129" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.268em;">0.7</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.252em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.079em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.088em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-17">r=0.7</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. The fabricated antenna is fed through a balun that consists of a high-pass filter, a low-pass filter, and a T-junction. Both filters have the fifth-order butterworth function. The balun has impedance of 50 <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-18-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-130" role="math" style="width: 0.929em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.731em; height: 0px; font-size: 126%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.326em 1000.66em 2.45em -999.997em); top: -2.245em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-131"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-132"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-133"></span></span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-134" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Ω</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.252em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.079em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.088em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-18">{}\Omega</script></tex-math></inline-formula> for the balanced port and 50 <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-19-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-135" role="math" style="width: 0.929em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.731em; height: 0px; font-size: 126%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.326em 1000.66em 2.45em -999.997em); top: -2.245em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-136"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-137"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-138"></span></span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-139" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Ω</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.252em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.079em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.088em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-19">{}\Omega</script></tex-math></inline-formula> for the unbalanced port. The balun introduces a small extra loss of about 0.4 dB. An equivalent series resistance (ESR) of 577 and 660 m<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-20-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-140" role="math" style="width: 0.929em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.731em; height: 0px; font-size: 126%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.326em 1000.66em 2.45em -999.997em); top: -2.245em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-141"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-142"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-143"></span></span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-144" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Ω</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.252em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.079em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.088em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-20">{}\Omega</script></tex-math></inline-formula> for the capacitors and inductors, respectively, is considered. Units are in millimeters.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6203553/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>

<div class="section" id="sec3"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION III.</div><h2>Far-Field UHF RFID Application</h2></div><p><a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig2" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 2</a> shows the simulated and measured return loss performance for the proposed antenna. It also shows the simulated surface current distribution. Numerical simulations were performed using the commercial simulator CST 2011.</p><p>
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig2"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/6170612/6203553/6203553-fig-2-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/6170612/6203553/6203553-fig-2-small.gif" alt="Figure 2" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 2. </b><fig><p>Simulated (solid line) and measured (open symbol) return loss for the four-unit-cell left-handed loop antenna. The inset shows the current distribution at the <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-21-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-145" role="math" style="width: 2.847em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.252em; height: 0px; font-size: 126%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.392em 1002.19em 2.45em -999.997em); top: -2.245em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-146"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-147"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-148"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-149" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">n</span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-150" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.268em;">=</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-151" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.268em;">0</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.252em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.079em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.004em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-21">{n}=0</script></tex-math></inline-formula> resonance.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6203553/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div><p></p><p>Four different operation modes can be observed. These can be understood by considering conventional resonance numbering, where the first and second resonances correspond to the left-handed region (negative resonances), the third resonance is attributed to the <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-22-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-152" role="math" style="width: 2.766em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.465em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.384em 1002.4em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-153"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-154"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-155"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-156" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">n</span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-157" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">=</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-158" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">0</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-22">{n}=0</script></tex-math></inline-formula> mode, and the last resonance is related to the right-handed region (positive resonances). The left-handed resonances appear at lower frequencies than the right-handed ones. The <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-23-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-159" role="math" style="width: 3.607em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 3.246em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.384em 1003.19em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-160"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-161"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-162"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-163" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">n</span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-164" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">=</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-165" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">−</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-166" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">2</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-23">{n}=-2</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-24-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-167" role="math" style="width: 3.607em; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-24">{n}=-4</script></tex-math></inline-formula> modes are observed at around 175 and 200 MHz according to simulation, and at 200 and 255MHz according to measurement. Similarly, the <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-25-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-175" role="math" style="width: 2.766em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.465em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.384em 1002.4em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-176"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-177"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-178"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-179" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">n</span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-180" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">=</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-181" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">2</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-25">{n}=2</script></tex-math></inline-formula> mode is found at 1110 MHz according to simulation and 1200 MHz according to measurement. An additional resonance is observed in the <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-26-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-182" role="math" style="width: 1.565em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.384em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.264em 1001.38em 2.465em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-183"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-184"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.384em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1000.66em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-185" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">S<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.604em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-186"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-187"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-188" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">11</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.197em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-26">S_{11}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>-parameter between the left- and right-handed resonances. This occurs at 868 MHz according to simulation and at 886 MHz according to measurement. It corresponds to the <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-27-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-189" role="math" style="width: 2.766em; top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-197"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-198"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-199"></span></span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-200" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">β<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; It is important to note that the <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-29-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-201" role="math" style="width: 2.766em; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.664em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-212"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-213"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-214" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">L</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.197em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-30">L_{\rm L}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-31-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-215" role="math" style="width: 1.444em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.264em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.264em 1001.26em 2.465em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-216"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-217"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.264em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1000.78em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-218" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">C<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.724em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-219"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-220"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-221" style="font-size: 70.7%;
