<p></p><p>Simulations show that the efficiency and directivity are 84.6% and 2.16 dBi for the <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-68-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-507" role="math" style="width: 2.766em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.465em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.384em 1002.4em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-508"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-509"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-510"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-511" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">n</span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-512" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">=</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-513" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">0</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-68">{n}=0</script></tex-math></inline-formula> mode and 84.3% and 3.04dBi for the <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-69-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-514" role="math" style="width: 2.766em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.465em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.384em 1002.4em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-515"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-516"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-517"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-518" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">n</span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-519" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">=</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-520" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">2</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-69">{n}=2</script></tex-math></inline-formula> mode. It is worth mentioning that in the case of the <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-70-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-521" role="math" style="width: 2.766em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.465em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.384em 1002.4em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-522"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-523"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-524"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-525" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">n</span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-526" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">=</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-527" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">0</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-70">{n}=0</script></tex-math></inline-formula> mode, efficiency is bigger compared to that of the previous design.</p></div>
<div class="section" id="sec4"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION IV.</div><h2>Near-Field UHF RFID Application</h2></div><p>Generally, loop antennas with good magnetic properties have been used as reader antennas in RFID systems. An inductive coupling system is preferred for these applications since most of the reactive energy is stored in the magnetic field. However, at the UHF band, the electrical size of the antenna loop becomes comparable to the operating wavelength, and it cannot produce a uniform magnetic field. As a result, these antennas produce a weak and nonuniform field distribution at the center of the loop <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref5" id="context_ref_5_4">[5]</a>–<a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref6" id="context_ref_6_4">[6]</a><a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref7" id="context_ref_7_4">[7]</a>. In this regard, these problems can be alleviated by metamaterial-based antennas working at <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-71-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-528" role="math" style="width: 2.766em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.465em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.384em 1002.4em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-529"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-530"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-531"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-532" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">n</span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-533" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">=</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-534" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">0</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-71">{n}=0</script></tex-math></inline-formula> mode. For this purpose, the inductively near-field of the loop antenna described in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig1" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 1</a> is analyzed. In this particular case, the distance between the inner and the outer loop is <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-72-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-535" role="math" style="width: 3.246em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.886em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1002.89em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-536"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-537"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-538"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-539" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">d<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-540" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">=</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-541" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">34</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-72">{d}=34 </script></tex-math></inline-formula>mm, and the load inductance <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-73-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-542" role="math" style="width: 1.324em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.204em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1001.2em 2.465em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-543"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-544"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.204em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.66em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-545" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">L</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.664em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-546"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-547"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-548" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">L</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.197em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-73">L_{\rm L}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is just due to the self-inductance provided by the strip that connects both loops. <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig6" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 6</a> shows the <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-74-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-549" role="math" style="width: 0.544em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.483em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.565em 1000.48em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-550"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-551" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">y<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-74">y</script></tex-math></inline-formula>-axis variation at <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-75-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-552" role="math" style="width: 3.486em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 3.126em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.384em 1003.07em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-553"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-554"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-555"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-556" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">z<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-557" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">=</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-558" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">0.5</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-75">{z}=0.5 </script></tex-math></inline-formula>mm of the magnetic field for the metamaterial loop antenna and a solid loop antenna with the same dimensions.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig6"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/6170612/6203553/6203553-fig-6-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/6170612/6203553/6203553-fig-6-small.gif" alt="Figure 6" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 6. </b><fig><p>Simulated magnetic field distribution of the proposed loop antenna in the <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-76-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-559" role="math" style="width: 0.599em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.466em; height: 0px; font-size: 126%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.524em 1000.47em 2.583em -999.997em); top: -2.179em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-560"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-561" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">y<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.186em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.329em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.004em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-76">y</script></tex-math></inline-formula>-axis (rotated 45° with respect to <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig1" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 1</a>) variation. <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-77-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-562" role="math" style="width: 3.575em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.847em; height: 0px; font-size: 126%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.392em 1002.78em 2.45em -999.997em); top: -2.245em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-563"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-564"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-565"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-566" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">z<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-567" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.268em;">=</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-568" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.268em;">0.5</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.252em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.079em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.004em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-77">{z}=0.5 </script></tex-math></inline-formula>mm.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6203553/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p><p>It is observed that the magnetic field features stronger magnitude in the regions close to the loop lines. Nevertheless, the magnetic field becomes flat along the <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-78-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-569" role="math" style="width: 0.544em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.483em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.565em 1000.48em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-570"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-571" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">y<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-78">y</script></tex-math></inline-formula>-direction in the major portion of the interior zone with low attenuation (minimum value of −4.7 dB). The <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-79-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-572" role="math" style="width: 0.664em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.604em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.565em 1000.54em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-573"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-574" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">x</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.67em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-79">x</script></tex-math></inline-formula>-direction presents similar results. On the contrary, the solid-loop antenna suffers a strong H-field attenuation of −47 dB. The magnitude of the magnetic field close to the center becomes negligible. In order to deeply analyze the performance of the proposed passive UHF near-field reader antenna, a comparative study of different conventional reader antenna configurations working at the UHF band is carried out. The antennas compared are the proposed loop antenna, a solid loop antenna with the same dimensions of our loop, the loop antenna described in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref5" id="context_ref_5_4">[5]</a>, the two segmented loop antennas described in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref6" id="context_ref_6_4">[6]</a> and <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref7" id="context_ref_7_4">[7]</a>, and the solid loop antenna described in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref7" id="context_ref_7_4">[7]</a>. The dimensions of the antennas presented in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref5" id="context_ref_5_4">[5]</a>–<a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref6" id="context_ref_6_4">[6]</a><a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref7" id="context_ref_7_4">[7]</a> are larger than the proposed loop size. <a ref-type="table" anchor="table2" class="fulltext-link">Table II</a> lists the simulated input impedance, directivity, radiation, and total efficiency, as well as the lowest strength field magnitude achieved.
</p><div class="figure figure-full table" id="table2"><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Table II </b>Comparative Study of the Near-Field UHF Loop Antenna Working at the <span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-80-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-575" role="math" style="width: 2.847em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.252em; height: 0px; font-size: 126%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.392em 1002.19em 2.45em -999.997em); top: -2.245em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-576"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-577"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-578"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-579" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">n</span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-580" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.268em;">=</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-581" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.268em;">0</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.252em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.079em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.004em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-80">{n}=0</script> Mode<div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></div><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/6170612/6203553/6203553-table-2-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/6170612/6203553/6203553-table-2-small.gif" alt="Table " /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div></div>
<p></p><p>The left-handed loop exhibits the best input impedance of 50 <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-81-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-582" role="math" style="width: 0.844em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.724em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1000.66em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-583"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-584"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-585"></span></span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-586" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Ω</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-81">{}\Omega</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and the best total efficiency of 84.1%, even if loading elements with higher losses are employed. Matching circuits are required for the rest of the antennas in order to obtain efficiency values higher than 90%. All antennas are low-gain. Concerning the near H-field distribution, the proposed loop antenna has the lowest attenuation value. It is at least 100 times lower than the segmented loop antennas and 10 000 times lower than the solid loop antennas.</p></div>
<div class="section" id="sec5"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION V.</div><h2>Conclusion</h2></div><p>In this letter, a novel compact loop antenna for near/far-field RFID applications is presented. The design is based on a transmission line with left-handed loading by means of two series capacitances and a shunt inductance. The antenna has zero phase constant at 868 MHz, thus giving an omnidirectional pattern in the plane of the loop. The left-handed loop reader antenna offers improved performances as reconfigurable or optimized responses can easily be achieved. Also, the proposed loop antenna has demonstrated the capability of producing strong magnetic field with relatively uniform distributions in the near-field region of the antenna. This sort of study sheds light onto the potential uses of metamaterials since conventional and emerging technologies have been compared directly. Several possible applications for these metamaterial-based antennas can be foreseen in technologies such as RFID, automotive electronics, TV, and radio reception.</p></div>
</div></div>

<script>

function getCookie(name) {
	var nameEQ = name + "=";
	var ca = document.cookie.split(';');
	for(var i=0;i &lt; ca.length;i++) {
		var c = ca[i];
		while (c.charAt(0)==' ') c = c.substring(1,c.length);
		if (c.indexOf(nameEQ) == 0) return c.substring(nameEQ.length,c.length);
	}
	return null;
}

j$('document').ready(function(){
	if(getCookie('legacyUserName')!=null)
	{
		if(IBP_WS_ENABLED_FLAG){
		Modal.refreshLegacyAccountTransition('/xpl/mwLegacyAccountTransition.jsp');
		}
	}
});

</script>
